<div id="review_1984324466" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1984324466" />
    <a title="Mariah of the Night Court" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29456303-mariah-of-the-night-court"><img alt="Mariah of the Night Court" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585943105p2/29456303.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1984324466?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mariah of the Night Court" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mariah of the Night Court" href="/user/show/29456303-mariah-of-the-night-court">Mariah of the Night Court</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1984324466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16621776317183517203"><b>VERY GOOD, BUT NOT SATISFIED WITH THAT ENDING.</b><br/><br/><b>***Contains Spoilers***</b><br/><br/>I literally stayed up last night from 10:00 to 5:00 AM reading the last 500 pages of this book. I am drained. Anyways, before I start on the main points of why I deducted 2 stars from this book, let me list some reasons why I enjoyed it.<br/><br/><b>*</b> Lia went through some hardcore character development and never gives up on what she believes in. She truly cares about the civilians in the three kingdoms and never lets her loyalty falter. Lo</span>
  <span id="freeText16621776317183517203" style="display:none"><b>VERY GOOD, BUT NOT SATISFIED WITH THAT ENDING.</b><br><br><b>***Contains Spoilers***</b><br><br>I literally stayed up last night from 10:00 to 5:00 AM reading the last 500 pages of this book. I am drained. Anyways, before I start on the main points of why I deducted 2 stars from this book, let me list some reasons why I enjoyed it.<br><br><b>*</b> Lia went through some hardcore character development and never gives up on what she believes in. She truly cares about the civilians in the three kingdoms and never lets her loyalty falter. Loved her character.<br><br><b>*</b> Kaden's full history is revealed and I was hit with all the feels.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493591717ra/22632678.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>*</b> Traitors in the court get what they deserve (I'm talkin to you Viceregent and Chancellor)<br><br><b>*</b> Lia's sass when exposing those traitors when she was like "Ooh Viceregent, you look a little jittery, take some of this medicine you gave to my slowly dying father." and he's like "Uh nah bitch I'm good.". <br><br><b>*</b> The continued embracing of the Venden culture in Morrighan from Lia and Kaden<br><br><b>*</b> Lia and Kaden moments alone<br><br>Alright, so now it's time to make my points that I didn't like, and sorry in advance, but I'm gonna rant a bit.<br><br>I have shipped Lia with Kaden since The Kiss of Deception. To me, they have more chemistry than Rafe and Lia, especially in The Heart of Betrayal where I had high hopes that Kaden was going to be end game. Kaden had shared his scars and brutal past with Lia and has clearly shown that he believes in her and knows that she is able to protect herself. Lia had also embraced the Venden culture with him by her side. Now I realize that Kaden was the assassin that had taken her to Venda for the Komizar, but he had his reasons. I'm not saying they were right, but he certaintly does make up for it in this book by aiding her in her journey to Morrgihan and helping her warn the people of the upcoming war that the Komizar has brewing. <br><br>Now, let me share my views on Rafe, or should I say, King Jaxon. I admit, I do like him as a character and can see why Lia chose him in the end, but I have my complaints. <b>I don't know about any of you, but I tend to always compare books to ACOTAR/ACOMAF. Don't read the next section if you haven't read the ACOTAR series.</b><br><br>I'm just gonna say it guys, Rafe was way too Tamlin-like for my taste. At first, he starts off as a great guy and could easily see why Lia fell for him. However, in this book, a different side of him had surfaced when everyone went to Dalbreck. He started becoming very controlling of Lia and hardly let her voice her concerns to the council or to warn her people of the upcoming war so her kingdoms wouldn't be destroyed. Like Tamlin, he denied Lia of her freedom in his kingdom, always had a group of guards surround her wherever she went, and secluding her to her tent while he dealt with matters himself. There was this one scene where Lia and Dalbreck were arguing behind the closed doors of the council meeting (that everyone could clearly hear and eavesdrop on) and Rafe had called his guards on Lia to take her away to her room. He even had the nerve to tell his guards to drag her out if she didn't cooperate. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1480898380ra/21361407.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now that should have been a huge, blaring siren for Lia to get the fuck out of that relationship. It was unhealthy and I still can't understand how she still ended up with him. I understand that he ended up changing his mind and went to Morrighan after some time, but that still doesn't make up for it. I'm just relieved that they aren't married and never fulfilled the alliance, but are doing some sort of super long distance type shit. <br><br>Back to Kaden. It seemed like he was just brushed aside in this book with no explanation whatsoever, like he was some sort of minor character with a little POV tidbit here and there. In the second book, it seemed like Pearson was gonna do something great with his character, but I guess she just decided not to put in that kind of effort and brushed him off instead. In my opinion, Kaden was a better man than Rafe and I know that some of you will disagree, but he was the one that believed in Lia and stuck by her side.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493591236ra/22632605.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There were several times while reading this book that I was literally shouting “No!”, “Are you fucking kidding me?!”, and “Please don’t let this be a thing…”, all in relation to one thing: Kaden and Pauline getting together. <b>NOW WHY THE FUCK DID PEARSON GO AND DO THAT. I DON’T THINK I’VE EVER BEEN ANGRIER BY A COUPLING AS I AM RIGHT NOW. LIKE NO. NOOOOOOOOOOOO. IT WAS SO FORCED AND HAD ZERO CHEMISTRY WHATSOEVER. LIA AND KADEN HAVE GONE THROUGH SO MUCH TOGETHER AND SEEMED LIKE THEIR RELATIONSHIP WAS BUILDING UP INTO THIS BEAUTIFUL THING…..BUT THEN NOTHING. KADEN WAS BRUSHED OFF AND LIA ENDED UP WITH THE TAMLIN. CAN WE PLEASE HAVE SARAH J MAAS COME IN HERE AND REWRITE THIS BOOK PLEASE, SHE’LL UNDERSTAND. AND PAULINE?! I MEAN, SHE’S A LIKEABLE CHARACTER AND ALL, BUT SHE JUST SEEMS…. UNNECESSARY. SHE REALLY DOESN’T DO ANYTHING, SHE’S JUST….THERE. THIS “RELATIONSHIP” WAS WAY TOO FAST AND FORCED AND MADE ABSOLUTELY ZERO SENSE TO ME.</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1486897186ra/21958699.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There were seriously so many times where I thought Lia and Kaden were going to be endgame. All I wanted was for Lia and Kaden to marry and rule Venda together, but I guess we all can’t get what we want. <br><br>One final point, which is the upcoming war against the Komizar’s army. I was expecting this huge, exciting blow out, but all I got was a few pages of a quick, anticlimactic battle that left me unsatisfied at the last 95% of the book. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493591718ra/22632679.gif" width="300" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Anything before that had barely any action and most characters were just sitting around talking. It was still entertaining to me, but there could’ve been less of that and more action.<br><br>All in all, I am very glad I picked up this series and had a lot of fun reading it, even if the ending left me as unsatisfied as it did.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16621776317183517203" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2196723597" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2196723597" />
    <a title="booksnpenguins" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66222749-booksnpenguins"><img alt="booksnpenguins" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580407796p2/66222749.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2196723597?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="booksnpenguins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="booksnpenguins" href="/user/show/66222749-booksnpenguins">booksnpenguins</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=high-dark-epic-fantasy">high-dark-epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=period-aus-past">period-aus-past</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=shippity-ship-ship">shippity-ship-ship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=royal-binches">royal-binches</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2196723597" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5043252215635296259">After months spent in denial, after months spent keeping myself back from reading the last chapters of this book because it'd mean I'd be done with this series forever, I finally found the courage to finish it and...the tears are real.<br/>Whether they're joyful tears or sad ones, that's still to decide. <br/>With great regret, though, I must admit this book was good but <i>not that good</i>. I expected more. More character development, more plot depth, more... I don't know, more <i>The Remnant Chronicles-ness</i>, I g</span>
  <span id="freeText5043252215635296259" style="display:none">After months spent in denial, after months spent keeping myself back from reading the last chapters of this book because it'd mean I'd be done with this series forever, I finally found the courage to finish it and...the tears are real.<br />Whether they're joyful tears or sad ones, that's still to decide. <br />With great regret, though, I must admit this book was good but <i>not that good</i>. I expected more. More character development, more plot depth, more... I don't know, more <i>The Remnant Chronicles-ness</i>, I guess, which is what brought me to love the other books.<br />Don't get me wrong, the author delivered more than I could have asked for, but she probably delivered it the wrong way. There were parts I seriously couldn't fathom, and the anticlimatic ending turned me off completely. It felt forcedly raw and cryptic, just as it happened with, <i>ahem</i>, <u>that romance related thing you all know</u>. And, can we please agree that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[this book needed a proper ending?? I can deal with open-endings but this series deserved better than a 'do your thing and imagine what you want'. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />I also ended up not liking those characters I truly loved in the first two books.<br />*clenched fists* Damn you, Lia. I mean Book Lia, not Me Lia. Or maybe I mean both. Her for being such a %$§, and me for setting my hopes so high. <br />I'm not sad about this, I still enjoyed myself, but I just didn't feel it, didn't let it get under my skin. <br />I probably should learn not to trust series finales.<br />Oh, well. <br /><br />Rounding this up by half a star because, as trashy and disappointing as this was, this series <s>especially Rafe my sun and stars</s> will always have a huge place in my heart and it gave me so many beautiful memories. <br />And feelings, lots of them. <br />I'll probably give this another try in the future, but I'm sure nothing will beat the awesomeness of The Heart of Betrayal.<br /><br /><b>ACTUAL RATINGS 3.5/5</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5043252215635296259" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1336850944" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1336850944" />
    <a title="Alafiya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44560617-alafiya"><img alt="Alafiya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460842696p2/44560617.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1336850944?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alafiya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alafiya" href="/user/show/44560617-alafiya">Alafiya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44560617-alafiya?shelf=love-these">love-these</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44560617-alafiya?shelf=fav-heroines">fav-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44560617-alafiya?shelf=book-bfs">book-bfs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44560617-alafiya?shelf=oh-wow">oh-wow</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1336850944" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8969310599482788726">Saturday, 3:41 am:<br/>I feel like Mary E. Pearson has stirred all my emotions. Emotions that I just can't settle. All of them flying, howling, circling, tumbling and jingling inside me. I have no idea how I'll recover. I just hope I get back to normal soon. Real life seems boring one minute and exhausting the next. I am staring at the ceiling and constantly thinking about this book. Even music hasn't been able to remedy this hangover. I feel miserable. This series has ended. *sigh*<br/><br/>Saturday, 10:14 am</span>
  <span id="freeText8969310599482788726" style="display:none">Saturday, 3:41 am:<br>I feel like Mary E. Pearson has stirred all my emotions. Emotions that I just can't settle. All of them flying, howling, circling, tumbling and jingling inside me. I have no idea how I'll recover. I just hope I get back to normal soon. Real life seems boring one minute and exhausting the next. I am staring at the ceiling and constantly thinking about this book. Even music hasn't been able to remedy this hangover. I feel miserable. This series has ended. *sigh*<br><br>Saturday, 10:14 am:<br>… ( ͡°; ͜ʖ ͡°;) Rafe, is <i> The Best. </i><br><br>Sunday, 9:00 pm:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471258567i/20016310.jpg" width="480" height="331" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Doesn't feel like that. I guess I'll just have to <b>
  <i> "Regroup. Move forward." </i>
</b><br><br>Monday, 3:44 pm:<br>Sometimes you read a book that tugs at your heart's strings, occupies space in your mind. A book that teaches you something and makes you yearn for more. The Beauty Of Darkness is that book for me. With every twist and turn, I felt my heart twist and turn in synchronization. What Lia felt, I felt. What Rafe went through, he took me along. With every whisper of truth breezing past Lia, goose bumps rose on my arms. My heart drummed, shivers ran down my spine. And not just for Lia. For Rafe, For Kaden, for Pauline. For Sven, for Jeb. For all of them. I felt a connection to this book. When I finished it I felt full and satisfied but oddly hollow and empty as well. This is definitely one of my most fav series of all time.<br><br>This book has it all. Friendship, love. Pain and heart break. War and violence. Failure and victory. Trust, understanding, mistrust, loyalty. New beginnings and many losses. <i>Everything. </i><br><br>The writing is spellbinding. Every word floating and curling like a whisper on the wind. Every sentence carrying a deeper meaning.<br><br>The romance, not your average boring lust induced gibberish. Not average, period. It's, it's... beautiful ( ͡°; ͜ʖ ͡°;) And heartbreaking and overwhelming.<br><br>The plot is detailed, no shit. Well thought out and perfectly strung. Flowing with creativity. <br><br>The characters, love them all. Even the side characters. I am just so sad that this series has ended. I don't want these characters to just drift away like that. That's how real they all felt. How attached I got to them all. ( ͡°; ͜ʖ ͡°;) <br><br>There were moments where I was scared the end would devastate me, but it didn't. Sometimes Rafe and Lia got on my nerves but they were all just acting out of character. Loved how they were so dedicated to both their kingdoms and to each other. Moments where I was disappointed too <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I wanted a bit more of the Komizar.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> But in the end of the day that doesn't matter at all. <br><br>This book is almost 680 pages long but worth it. Not dragged or pathetically filled with this-could've-been-omitted scenes. Infact it's so fast-paced and brilliant it felt like it was too short.<br><br>Thank you Mary E. Pearson for this extraordinary experience. Surely, you have the gift too. Albeit of a different kind.<br><br>To all, paviamma.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="8969310599482788726" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1331068208" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1331068208" />
    <a title="Mar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24789726-mar"><img alt="Mar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576151145p2/24789726.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1331068208?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mar" href="/user/show/24789726-mar">Mar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24789726-mar?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24789726-mar?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24789726-mar?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24789726-mar?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1331068208" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17071573951639354769">I'm so, <i>so</i>, <b>so</b> sad. Wait, I need to cry.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1472395485ra/20188868.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Okay, time to recollect myself just to write this review. <i>Then I shall cry again.</i><br/><br/>This was such a disappointment. The Kiss of Deception was one of my favorite books of early 2015, and then The Heart of Betrayal came that summer and man, <i>that</i> was a great second book in a series. I was so pumped for this book! I bought it at full prize, <b>believing it would be the best 2016 read</b>, maybe just after Empire of Storms... And I was so wrong.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1472395485ra/20188869.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The <u>review will have some </u></span>
  <span id="freeText17071573951639354769" style="display:none">I'm so, <i>so</i>, <b>so</b> sad. Wait, I need to cry.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1472395485ra/20188868.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Okay, time to recollect myself just to write this review. <i>Then I shall cry again.</i><br><br>This was such a disappointment. The Kiss of Deception was one of my favorite books of early 2015, and then The Heart of Betrayal came that summer and man, <i>that</i> was a great second book in a series. I was so pumped for this book! I bought it at full prize, <b>believing it would be the best 2016 read</b>, maybe just after Empire of Storms... And I was so wrong.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1472395485ra/20188869.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The <u>review will have some spoilers</u>, so basically <b>if you haven't started the series I'd suggest you read the first two books and stop there</b>. You don't need this third book, skip it and create your own ending. It'd be better and the first two books deserve even awards. They are really great. And now, stop reading or I will spoil everything for you.<br><br>So. Why don't we start with the <b>
  <u>worst</u>
</b>:<br><br>Rafe.<br><br>Rafe was such a cute boy in the first two books. I believed he would be a perfect match for Lia if Kaden wasn't around finally. <b>I actually cared about him, but then he started being possessive</b>. And controlling. And just a basic a-hole. Like always, here are some fragments:<br><br><blockquote>(Lia is talking): You are not letting me go anywhere. Where I go and what I do is still my choice to make!<br>He didn't back down, and his eyes became molten steel burning me with their heat. "No."<br>I looked at him uncertainly. "What do you mean, <i>no</i>?"<br>"You can't go."<br>Ad incredulous puff of air escaped from my lips. "Yo can't stop me."<br>"You think not?" He stepped closer, his chest as imposing as a wall. His eyes glowed like a beast's. "Have you forgotten? I am the <i>king</i> of Dalbreck," he growled. "And I decide who comes and goes here."</blockquote><br><br>UHM, <b>EXCUSE ME?</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1472395485ra/20188870.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That's not the only time Rafe literally imprisons her. The whole book until the last 200 pages are Rafe controlling Lia and overprotecting her, which, as you know, means he won't let her make her own decisions. Fucking asshole, I tell you.<br><br>The good thing? <b>Lia knows that what Rafe is doing is completely wrong.</b><br><br><blockquote>Maybe there would be no dancing at all. At least not between Rafe and me. Kings and prisoners did not share dances, at least not in any world I wanted to be a part of.</blockquote><br><br>So you would think that Lia would be intelligent and sent Rafe to hell. But no. OH NO. Because they are <i>fucking meant to each other</i> and obviously will end together. FUCKING HEEEEEEEELLLLLLLL<br><br>Okay.<br><br>Calm down.<br><br>Let's continue with the lesser stupidities, shall we?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/614629.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>The <i>thing</i> between Kaden and Pauline was so wrong and unnecessary</b>. You know, I liked Pauline and I liked Kaden, and I wished for them both to be happy. So the romance wouldn't be a problem if it wasn't because it's completely obvious that Mary E. Pearson used it as an excuse for Lia and Rafe to be together and the readers happy. <b>*NEWS FLASH* not everyone needs to be paired with another person.</b> Please, writers, understand this. We don't want couples popping up everywhere, and especially if there isn't a single same-sex couple in the whole book. Like, that smells pretty bad.<br><br>And I wouldn't have a problem with the situation neither if the others books would have given me hints of a connection between Pauline and Kaden, but there wasn't <b>anything</b>. Like I said, <b>the romance popped up from nowhere and we, readers, are expected to accept it. Nuh-nuh.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457177179ra/18328006.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now, the war. The freaking war. The super-duper <i>awaited war</i>. 10 freAKING PAGES. With multiple points of view that changed every 10 phrases. Uhm, what?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1472395485ra/20188871.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Not gonna say anything else about that. <b>So anticlimatic.</b><br><br>And then we had 30 pages left, if not less. You know... Not everyhing is decided in a fucking war. But we should accept that and move on, because everything ends perfectly and ¿? <b>Ah, I was so done by this point that I didn't even care about the resolution</b>. Wait, what resolution? The predictable one? Yes, that one. Boys and girls, I knew how this book would end by page 100. <b>That's not how you write the end of a series full of plot twists, Pearson</b> :(<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392557476ra/8577583.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And I'm not gonna write any more because I'm getting so mad and frustrated it's not even funny. I'm so disappointed. Oh. Aw. <b>Now let me cry again.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1472395485ra/20188868.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>--------------------------------------------------------------------<br><br><b>MARCH 2016</b><br>688 pages? OH MY GOD.               >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18325914353746935093"><p>Buddy-read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1323238951' rel='nofollow noopener'>Katerina</a> & <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1564404778' rel='nofollow noopener'>Vira</a> (click on names to check girls' reviews *whispers* they are awesome, you won't regret reading them, I promise). So, we are planning to visit Dalbreck soon, right? (Kate promised we would go). And I would like to link <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1641482574' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sarah's review</a>. Though we didn't read this book together, <i>all the feels</i>, guys! You must read the review and feel them too!<br/><b><i> <blockquote>When we lose a battle, we have to regroup and move forward again. Choose an alternate path if necessary. But if we dwell on ever</blockquote></i></b></p></span>
  <span id="freeText18325914353746935093" style="display:none"><p>Buddy-read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1323238951" rel="nofollow noopener">Katerina</a> &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1564404778" rel="nofollow noopener">Vira</a> (click on names to check girls' reviews *whispers* they are awesome, you won't regret reading them, I promise). So, we are planning to visit Dalbreck soon, right? (Kate promised we would go). And I would like to link <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1641482574" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah's review</a>. Though we didn't read this book together, <i>all the feels</i>, guys! You must read the review and feel them too!<br /><b><i> <blockquote>When we lose a battle, we have to regroup and move forward again. Choose an alternate path if necessary. But if we dwell on every action we’ve taken, it will cripple us, and soon we’ll take no action at all.</blockquote></i></b><br />If you read or followed my previous updates, you are aware that I am not a fan of this trilogy, but nevertheless I enjoyed it a lot. I loved how Mary Pearson created her world, how she intertwined every story and past and present - the world-building is mesmerizing! <br /><br />- I loved how this trilogy was getting <b>better and better with every book</b> and the last one was indeed a crescendo . <br /><br />- I loved that there wasn't a love triangle; how <b>slyly and expertly the author deceived us</b> into believing there was one, but no, there really was not. <br /><br />- I loved how <b>the plot is so sly</b> in this book, you can't trust anyone and you have to check and double check your suspicions regarding characters you thought you trusted before. It's this kind of intrigue I love in books and probably it won't be a lie telling I enjoyed the "spy part" the most.<br /><br />- I loved that <b>we don't have villains or heroes</b> in here - everything is gray and everyone has their reasons to be one way or another.<br /><br /></p><p>At this point it's hard to write anything about this trilogy without spoilers, so do not read further if you haven't read the previous installments yet.<b> SPOILERS AHEAD! </b><br /></p><p>Above I mostly listed the things I really enjoyed about this book. By specifying them I can add that the part where Lia had to find out whom to trust in Morrighan court is my favorite. I did believe for a second the vice regent was telling the truth to Lia about him being unaware of Kaden's slavery. You fooled me good, Mary Pearson! I adore how tricky most of the scenes in that place were. My heart raced like crazy, probably as much as traitors' who were fearing Lia's exposure of them.<br /><br />The last battle, though, was a little bit anticlimactic. I expected Komizar to fight Lia; I expected Kaden will have a heart-breaking episode with Komizar; I expected a lot of things in an epic sized action-packed way, but after discussing this topic with my friends, I came to conclusion that the battle was more psychological, than physical: the villains are not as terrible and intimidating and sometimes words can be a better weapon, and ultimately I am more satisfied than not with the way things with Komizar ended, though I still wish there was a scene between him and Kaden - a some kind of closure. <br /><br />Now to the things that slightly disturbed me in this book. Kaden and Pauline. I just don't get how these two happened. One moment Kaden was in love with Lia, the next moment he started to think about Pauline. The thing is, it felt unreal and too abrupt. I can believe that one year later they have a connection and can even build love for themselves, but the beginning of them just wasn't there for me. <br /><br />Also, I wish we had more of Rafe's and Kaden's voices in the whole trilogy. All we've got were their POVs here and there and, though they were leading male characters, I didn't feel they really had a voice. Most things we perceived from Lia's perspective and Kaden &amp; Rafe were there almost all the time to show us Lia from the side. But I wanted the heroes to be part of the voice in the books, to have an alternative look at the world and its history. What I mean is we mostly got this:<br /><b><i> <blockquote>He gave Rafe and Kaden a cursory glance, then sighed. “They’re both healthy young men, and how shall I say this delicately … easily influenced by a pretty face.”<br /></blockquote></i></b><br />And the sad part, I wasn't really invested in the character's love affairs. I liked them as individuals and was glad we've got Kaden's development in the second book, and in this one we've got more Rafe and his struggles. Lia's character I liked the less, but still her development was impressive: from an uncertain girl to a confident woman. But still, Kaden and Rafe were in the books for Lia more than for themselves. Don't get we wrong, Lia and Rafe do have hot stuff going on in through out the book and I enjoyed it, but I wanted a more independent from Lia's perspective view on the boys.<br /><b><i><blockquote>“Were any losses worth the gains?” </blockquote></i></b><br />The answer to this question will be "yes". No matter the flaws this book had (and there were little of them) I believe the conclusion is great. Losses, love, friendship, self-identification, trust, betrayal - all these things were intrinsically woven into this book and made we feel. The last 40% or so were especially emotionally hard because so many things happened in that part: relatively short time spun and non-stop action. And still there is plenty space left to create more stories in this world, and show us through other/new characters' eyes. That is how grand the world Mary Pearson created. <br /><i> <b><blockquote>“This world, it breathes you in … it knows you, and then it breathes you out again, shares you.” <br /></blockquote></b></i></p></span>
  <a data-text-id="18325914353746935093" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2500887509" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2500887509" />
    <a title="Rae" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3264820-rae"><img alt="Rae" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516304743p2/3264820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2500887509?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rae" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rae" href="/user/show/3264820-rae">Rae</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2500887509" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13391035391028756308">WARNING: MILD SPOILERS FOR THE KISS OF DECEPTION AND THE HEART OF BETRAYAL!<br/><br/>There is nothing better than an epic finale to a story that you have become so invested in. After going through so much with these characters you’ve come to know, there are so many emotions tied into how things will wrap up and eventually end. I love when I pick up the last book in a trilogy and realize it’s HUGE! To me, this means that I will be able to enjoy the story for that much longer, because most of the time I rea</span>
  <span id="freeText13391035391028756308" style="display:none">WARNING: MILD SPOILERS FOR THE KISS OF DECEPTION AND THE HEART OF BETRAYAL!<br /><br />There is nothing better than an epic finale to a story that you have become so invested in. After going through so much with these characters you’ve come to know, there are so many emotions tied into how things will wrap up and eventually end. I love when I pick up the last book in a trilogy and realize it’s HUGE! To me, this means that I will be able to enjoy the story for that much longer, because most of the time I really don’t want it to end.  Mary E. Pearson did a really fantastic job with this final book in the Remnant Chronicles. I needed so much to put my heart at ease after reading the whirlwind of chaos that was the end of the second book, Heart of Betrayal.<br /><br />Upon opening to the first page, you pick up exactly where book two left off. There is no time lapse to try and figure out what happened in between books, and for this I am grateful. My heart could not have handled anything less. The intense way the second book ended left me reeling as to what could possibly happen. And then our poor crew of runaway royals has now been thrust back into the Cam Lanteaux in a race against time. They must find a way to make it back to their kingdoms to warn them of the great danger heading their way. But not everyone believes in this danger like Lia does.  She was the only one to see what the Komizar was truly up to, and as unbelievable as it might be, she must stop him at all cost.<br /><br />After having been through so much, Lia really has fallen into the path of royalty that she fought so hard to run away from in the beginning. But she realizes that it isn’t just about finding love, but defending your home and your people. And when she can’t leave her kingdom behind to fend for themselves, tensions arise. I found that Kaden really became a character that I was instantly drawn to, he grew immensely as well, after learning that what he’s known for so long wasn’t what he thought, he chose to go with his heart, and his heart lies with Lia. Meanwhile, Rafe is struggling with his own decisions that he is forced to make, whether Lia is by his side or not, he can’t let his people down. Together, all three must make some of the biggest decisions of their lives and for the better of the whole, or so they hope.  <br /><br />I was so happy with the way Mary E. Pearson did not leave a single character out, we learn about what is going on in all the kingdoms we have visited throughout this journey, each character’s story is wrapped up, there are no loose ends left to wonder what might have happened. This to me is a sign of a great book, there’s nothing less satisfying than getting so far involved in a series only to be left hanging at the end. The story was unputdownable and I couldn’t tear my eyes away from the pages. I sacrificed sleep along with the characters, I felt their exhaustion and worry and passion to make it to their next destination and to save their people from danger and death. I felt the love that has grown between the characters, and the friendships that they have bonded. I never wanted this to end, but even though it did, I was so very happy with the ending. There were so many unknowns from the previous books as well that were explained in this final installment and there really isn’t a question left unanswered except for what might happen to these characters in the future. What I wouldn’t give to have another trilogy with my beloved trio.  <br /><br />This world, and these characters, and this book were such a fun journey as a reader to experience. I am so glad that I took the plunge and read these and I will most definitely be adding these to my favorites shelf. There will be a reread in the future because I am not ready to let these characters go.  I don’t know what took me so long to read them, but I am so very happy that I did. Do me a favor, and yourself a favor while you’re at it, and give yourself the joy of reading these amazing books. Trust me, you wont regret it,.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13391035391028756308" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4505887241884582323" style="display:none">The Beauty of Darkness (The Remnant Chronicles #3), Mary E. Pearson<br /><br />Enjoyed The third and final book of the Remnant Chronicles series. I really liked how it ended.<br /><br />In this book, Lia has survived Venda—but so has a great evil bent on the destruction of Morrighan. And only Lia can stop it.<br /><br />With war on the horizon, Lia has no choice but to assume her role as First Daughter, as soldier—as leader. While she struggles to reach Morrighan and warn them, she finds herself at cross-purposes with Rafe and suspicious of Kaden, who has hunted her down.<br /><br />In this conclusion to the Remnant Chronicles trilogy, traitors must be rooted out, sacrifices must be made, and impossible odds must be overcome as the future of every kingdom hangs in the balance.<br /><br />تاریخ خوانش روز بیست و پنجم ماه ژانویه سال 2017 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: زیبائی تاریکی: کتاب سوم سری تاریخهای باقیمانده؛ نویسنده: ماری ای. پیرسون؛<br /><br />ا. شربیانی</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2680115976" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2680115976" />
    <a title="Prim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69595193-prim"><img alt="Prim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592225691p2/69595193.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2680115976?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2019</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69595193-prim?shelf=fav-2019">fav-2019</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2680115976" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16903644801088713068"><b>➸ 5 stars</b><br/><br/>The kiss of deception was one of my first YA fantasy books that I read and it is the book that get me into reading fantasy. I will miss all these characters so much. I just want to pickup Dance of Thieves now because I heard that there's the appearance of Lia in that book. <br/><br/>Overall, I think this is a very good series for those who want to start getting into fantasy genre and prefer political-intrigued fantasy books with great romance, great character development, great plot, great writin</span>
  <span id="freeText16903644801088713068" style="display:none"><b>➸ 5 stars</b><br /><br />The kiss of deception was one of my first YA fantasy books that I read and it is the book that get me into reading fantasy. I will miss all these characters so much. I just want to pickup Dance of Thieves now because I heard that there's the appearance of Lia in that book. <br /><br />Overall, I think this is a very good series for those who want to start getting into fantasy genre and prefer political-intrigued fantasy books with great romance, great character development, great plot, great writing and of course .. great ending (I think I will come back and reread the final chapter again cause it's just so satisfying).<br /><br />Favourite quote: <br /><i>“No matter how great a gift or skill, it’s impossible to foresee every outcome.”</i></span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LLikm10d0ZoUGpZsee7OYQIRG9eN03Y8YBajyfOu5ynmHM5g6cFGOePUmD2kv7ixqNr+Lo5LW4tNxzUbAckkLw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lz8HHSVuuyLcZK4BomhEZuVMc29epKpe9jVjffy6bBpdm23mkbIsgSuqoFB/OTK2T4eWll08h+nb5PWvDt2vHA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11907261861740431887">Mary E. Pearson is the NYT bestselling and award-winning author of eleven YA novels and one novella. Her works include the completed trilogy, <i>The Remnant Chronicles</i>, which in a starred review, Publisher’s Weekly called <i>“masterfully crafted.”</i> Her favorite activities as a child were climbing tall trees imagining she was a hero in some fantastical world, or running along fence tops and roofs pretendi</span>
  <span id="freeText11907261861740431887" style="display:none">Mary E. Pearson is the NYT bestselling and award-winning author of eleven YA novels and one novella. Her works include the completed trilogy, <i>The Remnant Chronicles</i>, which in a starred review, Publisher’s Weekly called <i>“masterfully crafted.”</i> Her favorite activities as a child were climbing tall trees imagining she was a hero in some fantastical world, or running along fence tops and roofs pretending she was a spy with a bagful of amazing gadgets. She was rarely herself. Amazingly, she never broke a bone until she caught a basketball in gym class. Catching real balls was not her forte. These days she continues to live in make-believe worlds she creates in her books. Her latest 2-book series, <i>Dance of Thieves</i>, allows her do all kinds of dangerous things without breaking any bones. So far. <br />You can learn more about Mary and her books at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.marypearson.com">www.marypearson.com</a><br /></span>
